# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Summary

I've identified and documented **12 key Go source files** from the etcd-io/etcd repository that implement client-side retry and timeout policy:

### Core Components Found:

1. **gRPC Retry Interceptor** (`client/v3/retry_interceptor.go`): Implements both unary and streaming retry logic with configurable backoff and jitter

2. **Client Connection Management** (`client/v3/client.go`): Sets up interceptors, keepalive parameters, and health checks for connections

3. **Safe Retry Logic** (`client/v3/retry.go`): Distinguishes between safe retry scenarios for mutable (KV Put/Delete) vs immutable (Get) operations

4. **Watch Implementation** (`client/v3/watch.go`): Provides long-lived streaming with auto-reconnection and watcher resumption

5. **Lease Keep-Alive** (`client/v3/lease.go`): Manages automatic lease renewal with stream-based keep-alive

6. **Endpoint Resolver** (`client/v3/internal/resolver/resolver.go`): Implements gRPC resolver with round-robin load balancing

7. **Configuration** (`client/v3/config.go`, `options.go`): Defines configurable timeouts, retry limits, and backoff parameters

All findings are documented in `/workspace/answer.json` with:
- **Files list**: 12 implementation files
- **Symbols list**: 24 key functions, types, and methods
- **Call chain**: Shows interaction flow from client initialization through RPCs
- **Detailed narrative**: Comprehensive explanation of retry policy, backoff strategy, and timeout enforcement for KV, Watch, and Lease operations

implements a comprehensive client-side retry and timeout policy for gRPC operations in the GitHub repository github.com/etcd-io/etcd. The implementation spans multiple files in the client/v3 package and provides different retry strategies for KV, Watch, and Lease operations.\\n\\n## Core Components\\n\\n### 1. gRPC Retry Interceptor (client/v3/retry_interceptor.go)\\n\\nThe retry interceptor is the main component handling retry logic for both unary and streaming RPCs:\\n\\n- **unaryClientInterceptor** (line 41): Returns a new retrying unary client interceptor that handles retry for non-streaming calls. It implements:\\n  - Automatic retry on transient errors\\n  - Exponential backoff with jitter\\n  - Token refresh on authentication failures\\n  - Peer tracking for debugging\\n\\n- **streamClientInterceptor** (line 112): Returns a new retrying stream client interceptor for server-side streaming (1:n) calls. It:\\n  - Supports retry only for ServerStreams (not ClientStreams or BidiStreams)\\n  - Buffers messages to support retry\\n  - Reestablishes streams on errors\\n\\n- **serverStreamingRetryingStream** (line 188): Implements the actual retry logic for streaming responses:\\n  - Tracks buffered sends and received messages\\n  - Implements RecvMsg with retry capability\\n  - Reestablishes stream and resends buffered messages on failure\\n\\n- **isSafeRetry** (line 330): Determines if a request is safe for retry based on error type and retry policy (repeatable vs nonRepeatable)\\n\\n- **waitRetryBackoff** (line 312): Handles backoff timing between retries using context-aware waiting\\n\\n- **backoffLinearWithJitter** (line 446): Creates a backoff function that applies linear backoff with configurable jitter\\n\\n### 2. Client Connection and Initialization (client/v3/client.go)\\n\\nThe main client handles connection setup with integrated retry policies:\\n\\n- **newClient** (line 408): Initializes the client with:\\n  - Connection establishment via dialWithBalancer\\n  - Integration of retry interceptors\\n  - Health check via waitForConnection\\n  - Token/authentication setup\\n\\n- **dialSetupOpts** (line 229): Configures dial options including:\\n  - Keepalive parameters (DialKeepAliveTime, DialKeepAliveTimeout)\\n  - Unary and stream retry interceptors with configurable limits and backoff\\n  - Default: 100 max unary retries with 25ms backoff and 10% jitter\\n\\n- **waitForConnection** (line 345): Performs health check on the gRPC connection using gRPC health service:\\n  - Uses grpc.WaitForReady(true) for robust checking\\n  - Handles Unimplemented and FailedPrecondition gracefully\\n  - Validates connection is ready before returning\\n\\n- **roundRobinQuorumBackoff** (line 537): Implements round-robin aware backoff strategy:\\n  - Applies backoff only after cycling through the quorum\\n  - Uses jitterUp function to add randomness\\n  - Optimizes retry efficiency in multi-endpoint scenarios\\n\\n### 3. Safe Retry Logic (client/v3/retry.go)\\n\\nThe retry module distinguishes between safe retry scenarios for different RPC types:\\n\\n- **isSafeRetryImmutableRPC** (line 54): For immutable requests (e.g., Get, Range):\\n  - Safe to retry on Unavailable errors\\n  - Not safe for other server errors (e.g., ErrCompacted)\\n  - Retries on transient connection failures\\n\\n- **isSafeRetryMutableRPC** (line 85): For mutable requests (e.g., Put, Delete, Txn):\\n  - Only safe to retry on Unavailable when no connection is established\\n  - Protects write-at-most-once semantics\\n  - Checks for specific error descriptions indicating no available addresses\\n\\n- **RetryKVClient** (line 101): Wraps KV client operations with appropriate retry policies:\\n  - Range/Get: repeatable policy (safe to retry)\\n  - Put/Delete/Txn: nonRepeatable policy (restricted retry)\\n\\n- **RetryLeaseClient** (line 132): Wraps Lease client operations:\\n  - LeaseGrant: repeatable policy\\n  - LeaseKeepAlive: repeatable policy (for stream retry)\\n  - LeaseRevoke/LeaseTimeToLive: repeatable policy\\n\\n### 4. KV Operations (client/v3/kv.go)\\n\\nThe KV interface defines core operations:\\n\\n- **Put** (line 39): Stores key-value pairs with gRPC call options from client\\n- **Get** (line 49): Retrieves values with optional range, revision, limit, and sort options\\n- **Delete** (line 52): Deletes keys with optional range support\\n- **Txn** (line 65): Creates transactions for atomic multi-operation requests\\n\\nAll KV operations use the client's call options which include retry configuration.\\n\\n### 5. Watch Implementation (client/v3/watch.go)\\n\\nWatch provides long-lived streaming connections with intelligent retry:\\n\\n- **watchGRPCStream** (line 157): Manages a single gRPC streaming connection:\\n  - Tracks all active watchers on the stream\\n  - Handles stream reconnection and watcher resumption\\n  - Implements buffering for watch responses (respc channel)\\n  - Manages closing and error handling\\n\\n- **newWatcherGRPCStream** (line 275): Creates a new watch stream with:\\n  - Context wrapping using valCtx for non-cancellable context (line 276)\\n  - Automatic stream lifecycle management\\n  - Separation of request/response channels for concurrency\\n\\n- **valCtx** (line 269): A custom context wrapper that:\\n  - Preserves context values\\n  - Never returns Done(), allowing watches to continue indefinitely\\n  - Returns a zero-time deadline and nil error to prevent cancellation\\n\\n- **Watch** (line 298): Initiates a watch with:\\n  - Request queuing to the watch stream\\n  - Automatic ID assignment for watch requests\\n  - Streaming response handling through watch channels\\n\\nWatch streams use the stream retry interceptor configuration (disabled by default but safe to enable individually).\\n\\n### 6. Lease Keep-Alive (client/v3/lease.go)\\n\\nLease management with continuous renewal:\\n\\n- **lessor** (line 151): Manages lease keep-alive streams:\\n  - Tracks active keep-alives for multiple leases\\n  - Implements automatic renewal via keep-alive loop\\n  - Handles stream reconnection with backoff\\n  - Uses retryConnWait (500ms) between reconnection attempts\\n\\n- **KeepAlive** (line 273): Establishes automatic lease renewal:\\n  - Creates a channel for keep-alive responses\\n  - Multiplexes multiple subscribers to the same lease\\n  - Implements deadline tracking for keep-alive deadlines\\n  - Uses defaultTTL (5 seconds) before actual TTL is known\\n\\n- **NewLease** (line 192): Creates a lease client with:\\n  - RetryLeaseClient wrapping for safe retry\\n  - KeepAliveTimeout = DialTimeout + 1 second\\n\\n### 7. Configuration (client/v3/config.go, client/v3/options.go)\\n\\nConfigurable retry and timeout parameters:\\n\\n- **Config.DialTimeout**: Timeout for establishing connection (default: configurable)\\n- **Config.DialKeepAliveTime**: Keepalive ping interval (default: configurable)\\n- **Config.DialKeepAliveTimeout**: Keepalive response timeout (default: configurable)\\n- **Config.MaxUnaryRetries**: Maximum unary retries (default: 100 via options.go line 45)\\n- **Config.BackoffWaitBetween**: Base backoff duration (default: 25ms via options.go line 53)\\n- **Config.BackoffJitterFraction**: Jitter percentage (default: 0.10 or 10% via options.go line 56)\\n- **Config.PermitWithoutStream**: Allow keepalive without active streams\\n\\n### 8. Utility Functions\\n\\n- **jitterUp** (client/v3/utils.go line 28): Applies random jitter to backoff duration:\\n  - Adds/subtracts time within jitter fraction\\n  - Example: 10s with 0.1 jitter returns time in [9s, 11s]\\n  - Uses cryptographic rand for unpredictability\\n\\n- **WithRequireLeader** (client/v3/ctx.go line 28): Adds metadata requiring cluster leader:\\n  - Ensures requests fail if no leader is available\\n  - Prevents watch streams from getting stuck on partitioned nodes\\n\\n### 9. Endpoint Management\\n\\n- **EtcdManualResolver** (client/v3/internal/resolver/resolver.go line 31): gRPC resolver for endpoint management:\\n  - Maintains list of endpoints and provides to gRPC\\n  - Uses round_robin load balancing policy\\n  - Updates endpoints dynamically via SetEndpoints\\n  - Integrates with auto-sync feature for cluster membership discovery\\n\\n- **Interpret** (client/v3/internal/endpoint/endpoint.go line 131): Parses endpoints:\\n  - Handles http://, https://, unix://, unixs:// schemes\\n  - Extracts address and server name for TLS certificate matching\\n\\n## Retry and Timeout Flow\\n\\n1. **Client Initialization**: newClient \u2192 dialWithBalancer \u2192 dial \u2192 dialSetupOpts\\n   - Registers unaryClientInterceptor and streamClientInterceptor\\n   - Sets keepalive parameters\\n   - Performs health check via waitForConnection\\n\\n2. **Unary RPC Request** (e.g., Put, Get):\\n   - unaryClientInterceptor intercepts call\\n   - Attempts request with configured retry policy\\n   - On error: checks isSafeRetry (uses isSafeRetryMutableRPC or isSafeRetryImmutableRPC)\\n   - Applies backoff (via roundRobinQuorumBackoff) using jitterUp\\n   - Retries up to MaxUnaryRetries times\\n\\n3. **Streaming RPC Request** (e.g., Watch, LeaseKeepAlive):\\n   - streamClientInterceptor creates serverStreamingRetryingStream wrapper\\n   - Initial stream connection via remote.Watch or remote.LeaseKeepAlive\\n   - On RecvMsg error: buffers sends and reestablishes stream\\n   - Applies same retry logic and backoff strategy\\n\\n4. **Watch Streaming**:\\n   - Watch context wrapped in valCtx to prevent cancellation\\n   - watchGRPCStream manages connection state\\n   - Auto-reconnection on errors with backoff\\n   - Watcher resumption after reconnection\\n\\n5. **Lease Keep-Alive**:\\n   - lessor maintains stream per client\\n   - Sends periodic keep-alive messages\\n   - Multiplexes responses to multiple subscribers\\n   - Auto-reconnection with retryConnWait (500ms) backoff\\n\\n## Key Design Principles\\n\\n1. **Write-At-Most-Once Semantics**: Mutable operations only retry on Unavailable before connection is established\\n2. **Health-Check Based Connection**: Uses gRPC health service to validate connections\\n3. **Intelligent Backoff**: Round-robin aware backoff to optimize multi-endpoint retry\\n4. **Configurable Retry Policies**: Different policies for immutable (repeatable) vs mutable (nonRepeatable) operations\\n5. **Stream Retry Support**: Buffering allows stream retry while preserving order\\n6. **Context-Based Timeout Control**: Leverages Go context for deadline propagation\\n7. **Leader Awareness**: Optional WithRequireLeader metadata for consistency requirements\\n\\n## Implementation Details\\n\\nThe retry interceptor logic (client/v3/retry_interceptor.go lines 41-101 for unary):\\n- Logs retry attempts with peer information\\n- Handles authentication token refresh on auth errors\\n- Respects context deadlines\\n- Implements exponential backoff with jitter\\n- Returns on context deadline or non-retryable errors\\n\\nThe stream retry logic (client/v3/retry_interceptor.go lines 234-258) in RecvMsg:\\n- Only retries if previous receives failed (not after successful reception)\\n- Buffers and resends client messages on reconnection\\n- Maintains receive state to detect stream errors\\n- Applies same backoff and retry policies as unary operations\\n\"\n}\n",

Handles http://, https://, unix://, unixs:// schemes\\n  - Extracts address and server name for TLS certificate matching\\n\\n## Retry and Timeout Flow\\n\\n1. **Client Initialization**: newClient \u2192 dialWithBalancer \u2192 dial \u2192 dialSetupOpts\\n   - Registers unaryClientInterceptor and streamClientInterceptor\\n   - Sets keepalive parameters\\n   - Performs health check via waitForConnection\\n\\n2. **Unary RPC Request** (e.g., Put, Get):\\n   - unaryClientInterceptor intercepts call\\n   - Attempts request with configured retry policy\\n   - On error: checks isSafeRetry (uses isSafeRetryMutableRPC or isSafeRetryImmutableRPC)\\n   - Applies backoff (via roundRobinQuorumBackoff) using jitterUp\\n   - Retries up to MaxUnaryRetries times\\n\\n3. **Streaming RPC Request** (e.g., Watch, LeaseKeepAlive):\\n   - streamClientInterceptor creates serverStreamingRetryingStream wrapper\\n   - Initial stream connection via remote.Watch or remote.LeaseKeepAlive\\n   - On RecvMsg error: buffers sends and reestablishes stream\\n   - Applies same retry logic and backoff strategy\\n\\n4. **Watch Streaming**:\\n   - Watch context wrapped in valCtx to prevent cancellation\\n   - watchGRPCStream manages connection state\\n   - Auto-reconnection on errors with backoff\\n   - Watcher resumption after reconnection\\n\\n5. **Lease Keep-Alive**:\\n   - lessor maintains stream per client\\n   - Sends periodic keep-alive messages\\n   - Multiplexes responses to multiple subscribers\\n   - Auto-reconnection with retryConnWait (500ms) backoff\\n\\n## Key Design Principles\\n\\n1. **Write-At-Most-Once Semantics**: Mutable operations only retry on Unavailable before connection is established\\n2. **Health-Check Based Connection**: Uses gRPC health service to validate connections\\n3. **Intelligent Backoff**: Round-robin aware backoff to optimize multi-endpoint retry\\n4. **Configurable Retry Policies**: Different policies for immutable (repeatable) vs mutable (nonRepeatable) operations\\n5. **Stream Retry Support**: Buffering allows stream retry while preserving order\\n6. **Context-Based Timeout Control**: Leverages Go context for deadline propagation\\n7. **Leader Awareness**: Optional WithRequireLeader metadata for consistency requirements\\n\\n## Implementation Details\\n\\nThe retry interceptor logic (client/v3/retry_interceptor.go lines 41-101 for unary):\\n- Logs retry attempts with peer information\\n- Handles authentication token refresh on auth errors\\n- Respects context deadlines\\n- Implements exponential backoff with jitter\\n- Returns on context deadline or non-retryable errors\\n\\nThe stream retry logic (client/v3/retry_interceptor.go lines 234-258) in RecvMsg:\\n- Only retries if previous receives failed (not after successful reception)\\n- Buffers and resends client messages on reconnection\\n- Maintains receive state to detect stream errors\\n- Applies same backoff and retry policies as unary operations\\n\"\n}\n",
